        <title>Electrolyte/Structure-Dependent Cocktail Mediation Enabling High-Rate/Low-Plateau Metal Sulfide Anodes for Sodium Storage | Nano-Micro Letters

    <meta name="dc.title" content="Electrolyte/Structure-Dependent Cocktail Mediation Enabling High-Rate/Low-Plateau Metal Sulfide Anodes for Sodium Storage">
    <meta name="dc.source" content="Nano-Micro Letters 2021 13:1">
    <meta name="dc.format" content="text/html">
    <meta name="dc.publisher" content="Springer">
    <meta name="dc.date" content="2021-08-17">

    <meta name="dc.rightsAgent" content="journalpermissions@springernature.com">
    <meta name="dc.description" content="As promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries, metal sulfides ubiquitously suffer from low-rate and high-plateau issues, greatly hindering their application in full-cells. Herein, exemplifying carbon nanotubes (CNTs)-stringed metal sulfides superstructure (CSC) assembled by nano-dispersed SnS2 and CoS2 phases, cocktail mediation effect similar to that of high-entropy materials is initially studied in ether-based electrolyte to solve the challenges. The high nano-dispersity of metal sulfides in CSC anode underlies the cocktail-like mediation effect, enabling the circumvention of intrinsic drawbacks of different metal sulfides. By utilizing ether-based electrolyte, the reversibility of metal sulfides is greatly improved, sustaining a long-life effectivity of cocktail-like mediation. As such, CSC effectively overcomes low-rate flaw of SnS2 and high-plateau demerit of CoS2, simultaneously realizes a high rate and a low plateau. In half-cells, CSC delivers an ultrahigh-rate capability of 327.6 mAh g−1anode at 20 A g−1, far outperforming those of monometallic sulfides (SnS2, CoS2) and their mixtures. Compared with CoS2 phase and SnS2/CoS2 mixture, CSC shows remarkably lowered average charge voltage up to ca. 0.62&amp;nbsp;V. As-assembled CSC//Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 full-cell shows a good rate capability (0.05 ~ 1.0 A g−1, 120.3 mAh g−1electrode at 0.05 A g−1) and a high average discharge voltage up to 2.57&amp;nbsp;V, comparable to full-cells with alloy-type anodes. Kinetics analysis verifies that the cocktail-like mediation effect largely boosts the charge transfer and ionic diffusion in CSC, compared with single phase and mixed phases. Further mechanism study reveals that alternative and complementary electrochemical processes between nano-dispersed SnS2 and CoS2 phases are responsible for the lowered charge voltage of CSC. This electrolyte/structure-dependent cocktail-like mediation effect effectively enhances the practicability of metal sulfide anodes, which will boost the development of high-rate/-voltage sodium-ion full batteries.">

    <meta property="og:url" content="https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4">
    <meta property="og:type" content="article">
    <meta property="og:site_name" content="SpringerLink">
    <meta property="og:title" content="Electrolyte/Structure-Dependent Cocktail Mediation Enabling High-Rate/Low-Plateau Metal Sulfide Anodes for Sodium Storage - Nano-Micro Letters">
    <meta property="og:description" content="As promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries, metal sulfides ubiquitously suffer from low-rate and high-plateau issues, greatly hindering their application in full-cells. Herein, exemplifying carbon nanotubes (CNTs)-stringed metal sulfides superstructure (CSC) assembled by nano-dispersed SnS2 and CoS2 phases, cocktail mediation effect similar to that of high-entropy materials is initially studied in ether-based electrolyte to solve the challenges. The high nano-dispersity of metal sulfides in CSC anode underlies the cocktail-like mediation effect, enabling the circumvention of intrinsic drawbacks of different metal sulfides. By utilizing ether-based electrolyte, the reversibility of metal sulfides is greatly improved, sustaining a long-life effectivity of cocktail-like mediation. As such, CSC effectively overcomes low-rate flaw of SnS2 and high-plateau demerit of CoS2, simultaneously realizes a high rate and a low plateau. In half-cells, CSC delivers an ultrahigh-rate capability of 327.6 mAh g−1anode at 20 A g−1, far outperforming those of monometallic sulfides (SnS2, CoS2) and their mixtures. Compared with CoS2 phase and SnS2/CoS2 mixture, CSC shows remarkably lowered average charge voltage up to ca. 0.62 V. As-assembled CSC//Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 full-cell shows a good rate capability (0.05 ~ 1.0 A g−1, 120.3 mAh g−1electrode at 0.05 A g−1) and a high average discharge voltage up to 2.57 V, comparable to full-cells with alloy-type anodes. Kinetics analysis verifies that the cocktail-like mediation effect largely boosts the charge transfer and ionic diffusion in CSC, compared with single phase and mixed phases. Further mechanism study reveals that alternative and complementary electrochemical processes between nano-dispersed SnS2 and CoS2 phases are responsible for the lowered charge voltage of CSC. This electrolyte/structure-dependent cocktail-like mediation effect effectively enhances the practicability of metal sulfide anodes, which will boost the development of high-rate/-voltage sodium-ion full batteries.">
    <meta property="og:image" content="https://static-content.springer.com/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Figa_HTML.png">

    <script type="application/ld+json">{"mainEntity":{"headline":"Electrolyte/Structure-Dependent Cocktail Mediation Enabling High-Rate/Low-Plateau Metal Sulfide Anodes for Sodium Storage","description":"\n                \n                  \n                    \n                  \n                  \n                    \n                  \n                  \n                    \n                  \n                \n               As promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries, metal sulfides ubiquitously suffer from low-rate and high-plateau issues, greatly hindering their application in full-cells. Herein, exemplifying carbon nanotubes (CNTs)-stringed metal sulfides superstructure (CSC) assembled by nano-dispersed SnS2 and CoS2 phases, cocktail mediation effect similar to that of high-entropy materials is initially studied in ether-based electrolyte to solve the challenges. The high nano-dispersity of metal sulfides in CSC anode underlies the cocktail-like mediation effect, enabling the circumvention of intrinsic drawbacks of different metal sulfides. By utilizing ether-based electrolyte, the reversibility of metal sulfides is greatly improved, sustaining a long-life effectivity of cocktail-like mediation. As such, CSC effectively overcomes low-rate flaw of SnS2 and high-plateau demerit of CoS2, simultaneously realizes a high rate and a low plateau. In half-cells, CSC delivers an ultrahigh-rate capability of 327.6 mAh g−1anode at 20 A g−1, far outperforming those of monometallic sulfides (SnS2, CoS2) and their mixtures. Compared with CoS2 phase and SnS2/CoS2 mixture, CSC shows remarkably lowered average charge voltage up to ca. 0.62 V. As-assembled CSC//Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 full-cell shows a good rate capability (0.05 ~ 1.0 A g−1, 120.3 mAh g−1electrode at 0.05 A g−1) and a high average discharge voltage up to 2.57 V, comparable to full-cells with alloy-type anodes. Kinetics analysis verifies that the cocktail-like mediation effect largely boosts the charge transfer and ionic diffusion in CSC, compared with single phase and mixed phases. Further mechanism study reveals that alternative and complementary electrochemical processes between nano-dispersed SnS2 and CoS2 phases are responsible for the lowered charge voltage of CSC. This electrolyte/structure-dependent cocktail-like mediation effect effectively enhances the practicability of metal sulfide anodes, which will boost the development of high-rate/-voltage sodium-ion full batteries.\n                \n                  \n                \n Object.defineProperty(exports, "__esModule", { value: true });
exports.headerWidgetClientInit = void 0;
var headerWidgetClientInit = function (getCartInfo) {
    document.body.addEventListener("updatedCart", function () {
        updateCartIcon();
    }, false);
    return updateCartIcon();
    function updateCartIcon() {
        return getCartInfo()
            .then(function (res) { return res.json(); })
            .then(refreshCartState)
            .catch(function (_) { });
    }
    function refreshCartState(json) {
        var indicator = document.querySelector("#ecommerce-header-cart-icon-link .cart-info");
        /* istanbul ignore else */
        if (indicator && json.itemCount) {
            indicator.style.display = 'block';
            indicator.textContent = json.itemCount > 9 ? '9+' : json.itemCount.toString();
            var moreThanOneItem = json.itemCount > 1;
            indicator.setAttribute('title', "there ".concat(moreThanOneItem ? "are" : "is", " ").concat(json.itemCount, " item").concat(moreThanOneItem ? "s" : "", " in your cart"));
        }
        return json;
    }
};
exports.headerWidgetClientInit = headerWidgetClientInit;

                <use xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-accesses-medium"></use>
            </svg>4706 <span class="app-article-metrics-bar__label">Accesses</span></p>
        </li>
    
    
    
        
            <li class="app-article-metrics-bar__item">
                <p class="app-article-metrics-bar__count"><svg class="u-icon app-article-metrics-bar__icon" width="24" height="24" aria-hidden="true" focusable="false">
                    <use xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-altmetric-medium"></use>

        <li class="app-article-metrics-bar__item app-article-metrics-bar__item--metrics">
            <p class="app-article-metrics-bar__details"><a href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/metrics" data-track="click" data-track-action="view metrics" data-track-label="link" rel="nofollow">Explore all metrics <svg class="u-icon app-article-metrics-bar__arrow-icon" width="24" height="24" aria-hidden="true" focusable="false">

                <div data-article-body="true" data-track-component="article body" class="c-article-body">
                    
                    <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Highlights" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Highlights</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content">
              
              
                <ul class="u-list-style-bullet">
                  <li>
                    <p>Nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases endow CSC anode with electrolyte/structure-dependent cocktail mediation effect, showing superior rate capability and evidently lowered charge plateau compared with CoS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture.</p>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                    <p>Alternative electrochemical processes between nano-dispersed different metal sulfides and Na<sup>+</sup> carriers effectively overcome intrinsic flaws of monometallic sulfide, responsible for the lowered charge plateau of CSC.</p>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                    <p>As-assembled CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cell shows high-rate capability, and high discharge plateau up to 2.57&nbsp;V, which is comparable to that with alloy-type anodes.</p>
                  </li>
                </ul>
              
            </div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Abs2" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs2">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs2-content"><p>As promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries, metal sulfides ubiquitously suffer from low-rate and high-plateau issues, greatly hindering their application in full-cells. Herein, exemplifying carbon nanotubes (CNTs)-stringed metal sulfides superstructure (CSC) assembled by nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases, cocktail mediation effect similar to that of high-entropy materials is initially studied in ether-based electrolyte to solve the challenges. The high nano-dispersity of metal sulfides in CSC anode underlies the cocktail-like mediation effect, enabling the circumvention of intrinsic drawbacks of different metal sulfides. By utilizing ether-based electrolyte, the reversibility of metal sulfides is greatly improved, sustaining a long-life effectivity of cocktail-like mediation. As such, CSC effectively overcomes low-rate flaw of SnS<sub>2</sub> and high-plateau demerit of CoS<sub>2</sub>, simultaneously realizes a high rate and a low plateau. In half-cells, CSC delivers an ultrahigh-rate capability of 327.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>anode</sub> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>, far outperforming those of monometallic sulfides (SnS<sub>2</sub>, CoS<sub>2</sub>) and their mixtures. Compared with CoS<sub>2</sub> phase and SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture, CSC shows remarkably lowered average charge voltage up to <i>ca.</i> 0.62&nbsp;V. As-assembled CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cell shows a good rate capability (0.05 ~ 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, 120.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub> at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and a high average discharge voltage up to 2.57&nbsp;V, comparable to full-cells with alloy-type anodes. Kinetics analysis verifies that the cocktail-like mediation effect largely boosts the charge transfer and ionic diffusion in CSC, compared with single phase and mixed phases. Further mechanism study reveals that alternative and complementary electrochemical processes between nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases are responsible for the lowered charge voltage of CSC. This electrolyte/structure-dependent cocktail-like mediation effect effectively enhances the practicability of metal sulfide anodes, which will boost the development of high-rate/-voltage sodium-ion full batteries.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure"><figure><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Figa_HTML.png?as=webp"><img src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Figa_HTML.png" alt="" loading="lazy" width="685" height="759"></picture></div></div></figure></div></div></div></section>

                                <div class="main-content">
                                    <section data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">1 </span>Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>With the merits of high capacity and low cost, metal sulfides have been recognized as promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Z. Hu, Q. Liu, S.L. Chou, S.X. Dou, Advances and challenges in metal sulfides/selenides for next-generation rechargeable sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 29(48), 1700606 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201700606
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e715">1</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Y. Fang, D. Luan, X.W. Lou, Recent advances on mixed metal sulfides for advanced sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 32(42), 2002976 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202002976
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e718">2</a>]. However, most metal sulfide anodes examined to date exhibit poor high-rate performance and/or voltage behavior that trends rapidly to relatively high values. The result is full-cells that only operate well at a low rate (≤0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub>) and maintain average output voltages typically ≤2&nbsp;V _ENREF_6 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Tang, Z. Zhao, X. Hao, Y. Wang et al., Engineering hollow polyhedrons structured from carbon-coated CoSe2 nanospheres bridged by cnts with boosted sodium storage performance. J. Mater. Chem. A 5(26), 13591–13600 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/C7TA02665J
                  
                " href="#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e724">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Tang, Z. Zhao, X. Hao, Y. Wei et al., Cellular carbon-wrapped FeSe2 nanocavities with ultrathin walls and multiple rooms for ion diffusion-confined ultrafast sodium storage. J. Mater. Chem. A 7(9), 4469–4479 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/C8TA10614B
                  
                " href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e724_1">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Xiao, S.H. Lee, Y.-K. Sun, The application of metal sulfides in sodium ion batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 7(3), 1601329 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.201601329
                  
                " href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e724_2">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="J. Wang, L. Wang, C. Eng, J. Wang, Elucidating the irreversible mechanism and voltage hysteresis in conversion reaction for high-energy sodium–metal sulfide batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 7(14), 1602706 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.201602706
                  
                " href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e724_3">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Q. Guo, Y. Ma, T. Chen, Q. Xia et al., Cobalt sulfide quantum dot embedded N/S-doped carbon nanosheets with superior reversibility and rate capability for sodium-ion batteries. ACS Nano 11(12), 12658–12667 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.7b07132
                  
                " href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e724_4">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="X.-W. Lou, Bullet-like Cu9S5 hollow particles coated with nitrogen-doped carbon for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 131(23), 7826–7830 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/ange.201902988
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e727">8</a>]. At this level of performance, such cells are only slightly better than a number of advantages in energy density over aqueous batteries (e.g., zinc batteries) but noncomparable safety to the latter [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Tang, X. Li, H. Lv, D. Xie et al., Stabilized Co3+/Co4+ redox pair in in situ produced CoSe2−x-derived cobalt oxides for alkaline Zn batteries with 10,000-cycle lifespan and 1.9-V voltage plateau. Adv. Energy Mater. 10(25), 2000892 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202000892
                  
                " href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e731">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="A. Eftekhari, Low voltage anode materials for lithium-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 7, 157–180 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2017.01.009
                  
                " href="#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e731_1">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="X. Li, Y. Tang, J. Zhu, H. Lv et al., Boosting the cycling stability of aqueous flexible Zn batteries via F doping in nickel–cobalt carbonate hydroxide cathode. Small 16(31), 2001935 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.202001935
                  
                " href="#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e731_2">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="D. Chao, W. Zhou, F. Xie, C. Ye et al., Roadmap for advanced aqueous batteries: from design of materials to applications. Sci. Adv. 6(21), eaba4098 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1126/sciadv.aba4098
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e734">12</a>]. Thus far, many studies on metal sulfide anodes still focus on the enhancement in reversible capacity, rate capability, and cyclability in half-cells. Even few studies concerning the properties of metal sulfide anodes in full-cells, most of them only roughly evaluate the performance of full-cells based on anodes instead of total electrodes. This could result in certain intrinsic flaws of metal sulfide anodes underrated [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="A. Eftekhari, Low voltage anode materials for lithium-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 7, 157–180 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2017.01.009
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e737">10</a>]. Therefore, from the perspective of full-cell, to solve the low-rate and high-plateau issues of metal sulfide anodes is crucial for the development of high-performance full-cells (Scheme <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Sch1">1</a>a).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="scheme-1" data-title="Scheme 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Sch1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Scheme 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view scheme" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/schemes/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Sch1_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Sch1" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Sch1_HTML.png" alt="scheme 1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="305"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="scheme-1-desc"><p><b>a</b> Prototype of full-cells. <b>b</b> Rate capability comparison of typical metal sulfide anodes in half-cells. <b>c</b> Discharge plateau comparison in full-cells with different metal sulfide anodes showing the merits of FMS/AMS ultrastructure</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view scheme" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/schemes/1" data-track-dest="link:Scheme1 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image scheme 1" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Different metal sulfides usually show electrolyte/structure-dependent electrochemical properties, offering valuable inspiration to rationally design new architectures and investigate their properties in proper electrolyte [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Y. Tang, Z. Zhao, X. Hao, Y. Wang et al., Engineering hollow polyhedrons structured from carbon-coated CoSe2 nanospheres bridged by cnts with boosted sodium storage performance. J. Mater. Chem. A 5(26), 13591–13600 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/C7TA02665J
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e772">3</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="K. Zhang, M. Park, L. Zhou, G.-H. Lee et al., Urchin-like CoSe2 as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 26(37), 6728–6735 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.201602608
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e775">13</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Y. Tang, Z. Zhao, Y. Wang, Y. Dong et al., Carbon-stabilized interlayer-expanded few-layer MoSe2 nanosheets for sodium ion batteries with enhanced rate capability and cycling performance. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 8(47), 32324–32332 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsami.6b11230
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e778">14</a>]. Compared with ester-based electrolytes, ether-based electrolytes can effectively inhibit3 the shuttle effect of polysulfides in situ formed during discharge/charge processes, thus more beneficial to obtain reversible properties of metal sulfides [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Z. Hu, Q. Liu, S.L. Chou, S.X. Dou, Advances and challenges in metal sulfides/selenides for next-generation rechargeable sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 29(48), 1700606 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201700606
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e781">1</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="K. Zhang, M. Park, L. Zhou, G.-H. Lee et al., Urchin-like CoSe2 as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 26(37), 6728–6735 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.201602608
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e784">13</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="S. Qi, L. Mi, K. Song, K. Yang et al., Understanding shuttling effect in sodium ion batteries for the solution of capacity fading: FeS2 as an example. J. Phys. Chem. C 123(5), 2775–2782 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.jpcc.8b11069
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e788">15</a>]. Ferromagnetic metal (Fe, Co, Ni, etc.) sulfides (FMSs) are very promising conversion-reaction anode materials widely studied for SIBs [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="C. Dong, L. Guo, H. Li, B. Zhang et al., Rational fabrication of CoS2/Co4S3@N-doped carbon microspheres as excellent cycling performance anode for half/full sodium ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 25, 679–686 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2019.09.019
                  
                " href="#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e791">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Z. Man, P. Li, D. Zhou, Y. Wang et al., Two birds with one stone: FeS2@C yolk–shell composite for high-performance sodium-ion energy storage and electromagnetic wave absorption. Nano Lett. 20(5), 3769–3777 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.nanolett.0c00789
                  
                " href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e791_1">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S. Li, W. He, B. Liu, J. Cui et al., One-step construction of three-dimensional nickel sulfide-embedded carbon matrix for sodium-ion batteries and hybrid capacitors. Energy Storage Mater. 25, 636–643 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2019.09.021
                  
                " href="#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e791_2">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Y. Tang, Z. Zhao, Y. Wang, Y. Dong et al., Ultrasmall MoS2 nanosheets mosaiced into nitrogen-doped hierarchical porous carbon matrix for enhanced sodium storage performance. Electrochim. Acta 225, 369–377 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.electacta.2016.12.176
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e794">19</a>]. Compared with conventional hard carbon or red phosphorous anodes, FMS anodes can display ultrahigh-rate capability (≥20 A g<sup>−1</sup>) in ether-based electrolyte, holding a great promise in SIBs (Scheme <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Sch1">1</a>b) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Li, Y.-S. Hu, M.-M. Titirici, L. Chen et al., Hard carbon microtubes made from renewable cotton as high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 6(18), 1600659 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.201600659
                  
                " href="#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e802">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="H. Jin, H. Lu, W. Wu, S. Chen et al., Tailoring conductive networks within hollow carbon nanospheres to host phosphorus for advanced sodium ion batteries. Nano Energy 70, 104569 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104569
                  
                " href="#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e802_1">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="K. Zhang, M. Park, L. Zhou, G.-H. Lee et al., Cobalt-doped FeS2 nanospheres with complete solid solubility as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 55(41), 12822–12826 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.201607469
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e806">22</a>]. However, FMS anode usually suffers from severe voltage hysteresis and high plateau (~1.9&nbsp;V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>), largely lowering the discharge plateau of full-cells (Scheme <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Sch1">1</a>c). From this point, mono-component FMSs seem to be difficult to meet the requirements for high-performance full-cells. So far, despite many relevant studies, most of them are inclined to ignoring the severe intrinsic flaws of FMSs, emphasizing to enhance capacity and cyclability. By contrast, another series of metal (Sn, Sb, Bi, etc.) sulfides (AMSs) with conversion/alloying-reaction mechanisms can show acceptable voltage hysteresis and relatively lower voltage plateau [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Liu, Y. Yang, X. Wang, Y. Dong et al., Flexible paper-like free-standing electrodes by anchoring ultrafine SnS2 nanocrystals on graphene nanoribbons for high-performance sodium ion batteries. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 9(18), 15484–15491 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsami.7b02394
                  
                " href="#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e814">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Z. Liu, A. Daali, G.-L. Xu, M. Zhuang et al., Highly reversible sodiation/desodiation from a carbon-sandwiched SnS2 nanosheet anode for sodium ion batteries. Nano Lett. 20(5), 3844–3851 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.nanolett.0c00964
                  
                " href="#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e814_1">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="X. Ou, L. Cao, X. Liang, F. Zheng et al., Fabrication of SnS2/Mn2SnS4/carbon heterostructures for sodium-ion batteries with high initial coulombic efficiency and cycling stability. ACS Nano 13(3), 3666–3676 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.9b00375
                  
                " href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e814_2">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="X. Xiong, G. Wang, Y. Lin, Y. Wang et al., Enhancing sodium ion battery performance by strongly binding nanostructured Sb2S3 on sulfur-doped graphene sheets. ACS Nano 10(12), 10953–10959 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.6b05653
                  
                " href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e814_3">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="L. Cao, X. Gao, B. Zhang, X. Ou et al., Bimetallic sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 hollow nanorods as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries. ACS Nano 14(3), 3610–3620 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.0c00020
                  
                " href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e814_4">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S. Dong, C. Li, X. Ge, Z. Li et al., ZnS-Sb2S3@C core-double shell polyhedron structure derived from metal–organic framework as anodes for high performance sodium ion batteries. ACS Nano 11(6), 6474–6482 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.7b03321
                  
                " href="#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e814_5">28</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Huang, X. Hu, J. Li, J. Zhang et al., Rational construction of heterostructured core-shell Bi2S3@Co9S8 complex hollow particles toward high-performance Li- and Na-ion storage. Energy Storage Mater. 29, 121–130 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2020.04.004
                  
                " href="#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e814_6">29</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="B. Qu, C. Ma, G. Ji, C. Xu et al., Layered SnS2-reduced graphene oxide composite: a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life sodium-ion battery anode material. Adv. Mater. 26(23), 3854–3859 (2014). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201306314
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e817">30</a>]. However, these AMSs always suffer from severe volume change during discharge/charge processes, resulting in poor rate capability and cyclability in ester-based electrolytes (Scheme <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Sch1">1</a>b). Owing to latent catalysis over the decomposition of certain ether, such AMSs remain scarcely investigated in ether-based electrolyte [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="X. Gao, X. Yang, M. Li, Q. Sun et al., Cobalt-doped SnS2 with dual active centers of synergistic absorption-catalysis effect for high-S loading Li-S batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 29(8), 1806724 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.201806724
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e824">31</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="M. Hu, H. Zhang, L. Yang, R. Lv, Ultrahigh rate sodium-ion storage of SnS/SnS2 heterostructures anchored on S-doped reduced graphene oxide by ion-assisted growth. Carbon 143, 21–29 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.carbon.2018.08.048
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e827">32</a>]. Encouragingly, by utilizing fluorine-containing sodium salt in ether solvents as electrolyte, the undesirable catalysis of AMSs can be effectively suppressed to allow a stable battery operation [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Y. Xu, W. Cao, Y. Yin, J. Sheng et al., Novel NaTi2(PO4)3 nanowire clusters as high performance cathodes for mg-na hybrid-ion batteries. Nano Energy 55, 526–533 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.nanoen.2018.10.064
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e830">33</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="J. Xie, Y. Zhu, N. Zhuang, X. Li et al., High-concentration ether-based electrolyte boosts the electrochemical performance of SnS2–reduced graphene oxide for K-ion batteries. J. Mater. Chem. A 7(33), 19332–19341 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/C9TA06418D
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e833">34</a>]. The good compatibility enables the investigation of electrochemical properties of FMS/AMS composites in ether-based electrolytes. In the multi-component metal sulfide anodes, each component functions as active material and mutually compete. Thus, the electrochemical behaviors of multi-component metal sulfides are comprehensive results from individual component. Given that exotic properties beyond rule-of-mixtures (cocktail-like mediation effect) in multi-component high-entropy nano-systems [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="E.J. Pickering, N.G. Jones, High-entropy alloys: A critical assessment of their founding principles and future prospects. Int. Mater. Rev. 61(3), 183–202 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1080/09506608.2016.1180020
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e836">35</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Y. Ma, Y. Ma, Q. Wang, S. Schweidler et al., High-entropy energy materials: Challenges and new opportunities. Energy Environ. Sci. 14, 2883–2905 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/D1EE00505G
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e839">36</a>], to construct new superstructures assembled by nano-dispersed FMSs and AMSs and to study their properties in ether-based elctrolytes, could be an effective strategy toward high-performance full-cells. Additionally, the poor conductivity of most metal sulfides makes them essential to further combine with highly conductive carbon materials. Such combination can endow rational architectures with fast ion/electron transfer, which is conducive to obtaining satisfactory electrochemical properties [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="K. Zhang, M. Park, L. Zhou, G.-H. Lee et al., Urchin-like CoSe2 as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 26(37), 6728–6735 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.201602608
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e843">13</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="J. Kim, M.S. Choi, K.H. Shin, M. Kota et al., Rational design of carbon nanomaterials for electrochemical sodium storage and capture. Adv. Mater. 31(34), 1803444 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201803444
                  
                " href="#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e846">37</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="P. Xiong, P. Bai, A. Li, B. Li et al., Bismuth nanoparticle@carbon composite anodes for ultralong cycle life and high-rate sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 31(48), 1904771 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201904771
                  
                " href="#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e846_1">38</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="C. Li, S. Wang, G. Wang, S. Wang et al., NH4V4O10/RGO composite as a high-performance electrode material for hybrid capacitive deionization. Environ. Sci. Wat. Res. 6(2), 303–311 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/C9EW00499H
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e849">39</a>]. So far, despite some studies pertaining to FMS/AMS composites, the certain agglomeration or phase separation between FMS and AMS remains unsatisfactory to investigate their comprehensive impact. Additionally, such studies mostly involved the electrochemical properties of FMS/AMS composites in carbonate-based electrolytes [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="L. Shi, D. Li, P. Yao, J. Yu et al., SnS2 nanosheets coating on nanohollow cubic CoS2/C for ultralong life and high rate capability half/full sodium-ion batteries. Small 14(41), 1802716 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.201802716
                  
                " href="#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e852">40</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="X. Wang, X. Li, Q. Li, H. Li et al., Improved electrochemical performance based on nanostructured SnS2@CoS2–RGO composite anode for sodium-ion batteries. Nano-Micro Lett. 10(3), 46 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s40820-018-0200-x
                  
                " href="#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e852_1">41</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="X. Liu, Y. Xiang, Q. Li, Q. Zheng et al., SnS2-CoS2@C nanocubes as high initial coulombic efficiency and long-life anodes for sodium-ion batteries. Electrochim. Acta 387, 138525 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.electacta.2021.138525
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e855">42</a>]. Thus, to study the voltage behavior of metal sulfide composites in ether-based electrolytes will provide a new perspective to pursue desired sodium storage properties.</p><p>Herein, CNTs-stringed metal sulfides superstructure anode assembled by nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases (CSC, C: CNT; S: SnS<sub>2</sub>; C: CoS<sub>2</sub>) is engineered to combine the merits of FMS- and AMS-type anode materials, aiming at simultaneously solving the dual-problems of poor rate capability/output-voltage characteristics (Scheme <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Sch1">1</a>b-c). The highly nano-dispersed metal sulfides in CSC show remarkable cocktail-like mediation effect, effectively circumventing intrinsic drawbacks of different metal sulfides. The ether-based electrolyte greatly enhances the reversibility of metal sulfides, which can inhibit the aggregation of homogenous metal sulfides, enabling a long-life effectivity of cocktail-like mediation. In half-cells, CSC delivers an ultrahigh-rate capability of 327.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>, showing remarkably lowered average charge plateau up to 0.62&nbsp;V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>, compared with CoS<sub>2</sub> phase and SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture. The as-assembled CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cell shows a good rate capability (0.05 ~ 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, 120.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub> at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and a high average discharge voltage up to 2.57&nbsp;V, comparable to full-cells with alloy-type anodes. Kinetics and mechanism studies reveal that the cocktail mediation effect largely boosts the charge transfer and ionic diffusion in CSC; along the diffusion direction of Na<sup>+</sup> carriers, alternative and complementary electrochemical processes between different nano-dispersed metal sulfides (SnS<sub>2</sub>, CoS<sub>2</sub>) and Na<sup>+</sup> carriers are responsible for the lowered average charge plateau of CSC. This exhibited cocktail-like mediation effect evidently improves the practicability of metal sulfide anodes, which will boost the development of high-rate/-voltage sodium-ion full batteries.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Results and Discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec3-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec3"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2 </span>Results and Discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec3-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.1 </span>Materials Preparation and Characterization</h3><p>The CSC was initially obtained by ion-exchange reaction between thiostannate (Sn<sub>x</sub>S<sub>y</sub><sup>n−</sup>) and cobalt-based zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-67) followed by annealing treatment (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>a). For an enhanced conductivity of the resulting CSC, the ZIF-67 particles (C-ZIF-67) are connected together (‘stringed’) by a network of CNTs (Fig. S1). Sn<sup>119</sup> NMR spectroscopy reveals that several tetravalent thiostannate species (SnS<sub>3</sub><sup>2−</sup>, SnS<sub>4</sub><sup>4−</sup>, and Sn<sub>2</sub>S<sub>6</sub><sup>4−</sup>) exist in solution and these are referred to collectively as ‘Sn<sub>x</sub>S<sub>y</sub><sup>n−</sup>’ (Fig. S2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="P. Nørby, J. Overgaard, P.S. Christensen, B. Richter et al., (NH4)4Sn2S6·3H2O: crystal structure, thermal decomposition, and precursor for textured thin film. Chem. Mater. 26(15), 4494–4504 (2014). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/cm501681r
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e948">43</a>]. Within the ion-exchange process, Co<sup>2+</sup> in ZIF-67 reacts rapidly with Sn<sub>x</sub>S<sub>y</sub><sup>n−</sup> species, forming a unique superstructure comprised of nano-dispersed CoS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub> phases. The overall reaction follows Eq.&nbsp;(<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="equation anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Equ1">1</a>):</p><div id="Equ1" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$$ {\text{Sn}}_{x} {\text{S}}_{y}^{n - } + {\text{Co}}^{2 + } \to {\text{SnS}}_{2} + {\text{CoS}}_{2} \;\;\left( {1 \le x \le 2,\;\;3 \le y \le 6,\;\;2 \le n \le 4} \right) $$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (1)
                </div></div><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Fig. 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig1" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure 1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="617"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p><b>a</b> Schematic illustration of fabrication process of CSC, inset (right) showing the reaction between ZIF-67 and Sn<sub><i>x</i></sub>S<sub><i>y</i></sub><sup>n−</sup>. <b>b</b> XRD patterns of CNTs and CSC. <b>c</b> Mass content of CoS<sub>2</sub>, SnS<sub>2</sub>, and CNTs in the CSC. <b>d</b> N<sub>2</sub> adsorption isotherm of CSC and corresponding pore width distribution. <b>e</b> FE-SEM images of CSC (inset displaying the core/shell structure of CSC). <b>f</b> TEM image of CSC and <b>g</b> TEM-EDS element mapping of CSC including C, Co, Sn, and S. HR-TEM images of <b>h</b> shell and <b>i</b> core in CSC showing co-assembly of nano-CoS<sub>2</sub> and -SnS<sub>2</sub></p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 1" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>b, X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns exhibit the diffraction peaks of CoS<sub>2</sub> (PDF No. 00-41-1471), SnS<sub>2</sub> (PDF No. 00-23-0677), and carbon, verifying their presence in the CSC. Compared with standard phase, the reflection for the (0 0 1) plane of SnS<sub>2</sub> registers a slight shift toward lower angles, implying an expanded interlayer spacing [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Y. Tang, Z. Zhao, Y. Wang, Y. Dong et al., Carbon-stabilized interlayer-expanded few-layer MoSe2 nanosheets for sodium ion batteries with enhanced rate capability and cycling performance. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 8(47), 32324–32332 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsami.6b11230
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1177">14</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Z. Hu, L. Wang, K. Zhang, J. Wang et al., MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayers as high-performance anodes for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 53(47), 12794–12798 (2014). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.201407898
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1181">44</a>]. The expanded interlayer spacing could be associated with the use of thiostannate precursor and low-temperature ion-exchange process. The ion-exchange reaction of thiostannate with ZIF-67 typically occurs at −5&nbsp;°C in 1&nbsp;h, where fast reassembly of SnS<sub>2</sub> results in the expanded interlayer spacing. Also, the relatively low annealing temperature (450&nbsp;°C) is beneficial to retain the expanded interlayer spacing of SnS<sub>2</sub>. The content of carbon nanotubes in CSC is obtained by thermogravimetric analysis (TGA), which is ca. 3.75 wt% (Fig. S3). By inductively coupled plasma-mass spectrometry (ICP-MS), the elemental content of CSC is analyzed, revealing that the mole ratio of Co/Sn/S is <i>ca.</i> 1.00/1.73/5.46 (Table S1). The corresponding mass content of CoS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub> in the CSC is 26.95 and 69.30wt%, respectively (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>c). The type-IV N<sub>2</sub> adsorption isotherms of CSC present an evident hysteresis loop, indicating the presence of mesopores (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>d). The corresponding pore width (inset) mainly centers in the range of 20–45&nbsp;nm. The theoretical capacity of CSC anode (C<sub><i>T</i>-CSC</sub>) can be evaluated roughly according to the equation: C<sub><i>T</i>-CSC</sub> = <i>x</i>C<sub><i>T</i>-CoS2</sub> + <i>y</i>C<sub><i>T</i>-SnS2</sub>, where <i>x</i> and <i>y</i> is the percentage content of CoS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub> in the CSC. The C<sub><i>T</i>-CoS2</sub> and C<sub><i>T</i>-SnS2</sub> are the theoretical capacity of CoS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub>, which is 872 and 1136 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Thus, C<sub><i>T</i>-CSC</sub> = 0.2695 × 872 + 0.695 × 1136 = 1024.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>.</p><p>Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>e exhibits field emission scanning electron microscopy (FE-SEM) images of CSC, which consists of carbon nanotubes-stringed core/shell architecture (inset). Such core/shell structures are greatly influenced by precursors, solvents, reaction temperatures, and concentrations (Figs. S4–S6). The content of SnS<sub>2</sub> in the CSC can be tuned to some extent by varying the concentration of thiostannate solution (Fig. S6). Transmission electron microscope (TEM) image shows the typical radial morphology of the CSC (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>f). Energy-dispersive spectrometer (EDS) elemental mapping yields a distribution of the elements C, Sn, Co, and S in the CSC, which correspond well with the TEM image (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>g). The details of shell and core were further characterized by TEM. The shell is actually composed of nanosheets (Fig. S7a). As displayed in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>h, high-resolution transmission electron microscope (HR-TEM) image clearly exhibits interplanar spacings of 0.248 and 0.615&nbsp;nm for CoS<sub>2</sub> (2 1 0) and SnS<sub>2</sub> (0 0 1) lattice planes, verifying such nanosheets assembled by nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> (red) and CoS<sub>2</sub> (blue-green). The TEM-EDS line-scan profiles show matched peaks with Co, Sn, S elements, further suggesting the superstructure of shell co-assembled by SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases (Fig. S7b). Corresponding to SEM image of CSC (inset), the core of CSC shows an abundant microstructure, in which the pore (green) can be observed (Fig. S8a). As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig1">1</a>i, HR-TEM image of the core also exposes the lattice planes of SnS<sub>2</sub> (0 0 1) and CoS<sub>2</sub> (2 1 0), which accord with the corresponding selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern (Fig. S8b). Such results verify that the core of CSC is also assembled by nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases. The CSC was further analyzed by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS). As shown in Fig. S9, compared with commercial CoS<sub>2</sub> sample, the high-resolution of XPS of Co 2p of CSC shows a <i>ca.</i> 0.45&nbsp;eV shift toward higher binding energy. Moreover, the high-resolution of XPS of Sn 3d of CSC also appears a 0.61&nbsp;eV shift toward higher binding energy. Such results imply the presence of chemical effect between CoS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub> in CSC anodes [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="S. Huang, M. Wang, P. Jia, B. Wang et al., N-graphene motivated SnO2@SnS2 heterostructure quantum dots for high performance lithium/sodium storage. Energy Storage Mater. 20, 225–233 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2018.11.024
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1318">45</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Y. Yang, X.-A. Yang, D. Leng, S.-B. Wang et al., Fabrication of g-C3N4/SnS2/SnO2 nanocomposites for promoting photocatalytic reduction of aqueous Cr(VI) under visible light. Chem. Eng. J. 335, 491–500 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cej.2017.10.173
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1321">46</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.2 </span>Half-Cell Properties</h3><p>The electrochemical properties of anode materials are firstly evaluated by testing half-cells with Na foil as counter electrode and ether-based electrolytes with fluorine-containing sodium salt. For comparison, commercial SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> powders with well-matched XRD patterns to standard phases are also tested (Fig. S10). Compared with the CSC, the N<sub>2</sub> isotherms of commercial SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> samples typically exhibit no evident hysteresis loop, whereby the corresponding pore diameter distributions display nonporous properties (Fig. S11). After initial three scans at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, mono-component metal sulfides (CoS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub>) and anodes composed of both compounds show gradually stabilized CV curves (Fig. S12). The initial CV curve of the CSC anode shows three oxidation peaks, which are associated with SnS<sub>2</sub> phase at 0.70–1.55&nbsp;V and CoS<sub>2</sub> phase at 1.70–2.10&nbsp;V, respectively. The reduction peak at 1.60–1.80&nbsp;V is correlated with the CoS<sub>2</sub> phase, while the peaks at 0.50–1.10&nbsp;V are linked to SnS<sub>2</sub> and formation of solid electrolyte interphase (Fig. S13a). In subsequent scans, the reduction peak related to CoS<sub>2</sub> gradually disappears, which could result from electrochemical activation of nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="C. Dong, L. Guo, H. Li, B. Zhang et al., Rational fabrication of CoS2/Co4S3@N-doped carbon microspheres as excellent cycling performance anode for half/full sodium ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 25, 679–686 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2019.09.019
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1364">16</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="K. Zhang, M. Park, L. Zhou, G.-H. Lee et al., Cobalt-doped FeS2 nanospheres with complete solid solubility as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 55(41), 12822–12826 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.201607469
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1367">22</a>]. As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig2">2</a>a, the activated CSC delivers a main oxidized peak potential range (0.75–1.65&nbsp;V), which is close to that of SnS<sub>2</sub> (0.80–1.45&nbsp;V) but remarkably lower than that of CoS<sub>2</sub> (1.30–2.18&nbsp;V) and SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture (1.25–2.15&nbsp;V). Correspondingly, CSC anode displays an average charge voltage of <i>ca.</i> 1.30&nbsp;V, which is close to that of SnS<sub>2</sub> but lower than that of CoS<sub>2</sub> (<i>ca.</i> 1.92&nbsp;V) (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig2">2</a>b). Compared with commercial SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture with average charge voltage of <i>ca.</i> 1.81&nbsp;V, CSC anode also shows evident low-plateau merit (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig2">2</a>c). This verifies that the construction of a superstructure assembled from nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases is crucial for lowering the intrinsically high plateau of the CoS<sub>2</sub> phase. Specifically, as shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig2">2</a>d, the introduction of nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> phase into CSC effectively lowers the intrinsic average charge voltage of CoS<sub>2</sub> up to <i>ca.</i> 0.62&nbsp;V. This in turn will translate to a higher plateau voltage for full-cells, thereby improving their energy density.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Fig. 2"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 2</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click"
