curves of CSC, commercial SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub>, and SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture. <b>d</b> Histogram showing the average charge plateau voltages of various anodes in half-cells. <b>e</b> Capacity/charge plateau comparison of different anodes. <b>f</b> Rate capability of CSC, commercial SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> in half-cells. <b>g</b> Rate capability comparison of different anodes. <b>h</b> Long-life cyclability of CSC anode at 1 and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> (<i>CE</i> Coulombic efficiency)</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 2" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Compared with other metal chalcogenide anodes, CSC exhibits obvious high-capacity and low-plateau advantages (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig2">2</a>e). Moreover, compared with commercial SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub>, and mixtures of the two, CSC shows a remarkably improved rate capability, ranging from 0.5 to 20 A g<sup>−1</sup> with a high capacity of 327.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>anode</sub> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig2">2</a>f). The corresponding discharge/charge curves are exhibited in Fig. S14. When tested with ester-based electrolyte, CSC shows similar CV curves to that in ether-based electrolyte, but the reversible capacity, to the same cutoff voltage, shrinks markedly (Fig. S15). In addition, compared with in ether-based electrolyte, the rate capability of CSC is greatly deteriorated (Fig. S16), along with an increased resistance of charge transfer (Fig. S17). Such phenomena suggest the key role of ether-based electrolyte in stabilizing metal sulfide anodes and realizing fast charge transfer, which could be associated with good compatibility between metal sulfide and ether solvent [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Z. Hu, Q. Liu, S.L. Chou, S.X. Dou, Advances and challenges in metal sulfides/selenides for next-generation rechargeable sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 29(48), 1700606 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201700606
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1502">1</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="S. Qi, L. Mi, K. Song, K. Yang et al., Understanding shuttling effect in sodium ion batteries for the solution of capacity fading: FeS2 as an example. J. Phys. Chem. C 123(5), 2775–2782 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.jpcc.8b11069
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1505">15</a>]. Evidently, the CSC anode effectively circumvents the intrinsic high voltage of CoS<sub>2</sub> and low-rate drawback of SnS<sub>2</sub> in ether-based electrolyte. Compared with other anode materials in half-cells, CSC also shows a remarkable high-rate capability (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig2">2</a>g, Table S2)_ENREF_12_ENREF_13_ENREF_14_ENREF_15_ENREF_16_ENREF_17_ENREF_18 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S. Wang, F. Gong, S. Yang, J. Liao et al., Graphene oxide-template controlled cuboid-shaped high-capacity VS4 nanoparticles as anode for sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 28(34), 1801806 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.201801806
                  
                " href="#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1516">47</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S. Li, P. Ge, F. Jiang, H. Shuai et al., The advance of nickel-cobalt-sulfide as ultra-fast/high sodium storage materials: the influences of morphology structure, phase evolution and interface property. Energy Storage Mater. 16, 267–280 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2018.06.006
                  
                " href="#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1516_1">48</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Li, R. Zhang, W. Zhou, X. Wu et al., Hierarchical MoS2 hollow architectures with abundant mo vacancies for efficient sodium storage. ACS Nano 13(5), 5533–5540 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.9b00383
                  
                " href="#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1516_2">49</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="J. Chen, L. Mohrhusen, G. Ali, S. Li et al., Electrochemical mechanism investigation of Cu2MoS4 hollow nanospheres for fast and stable sodium ion storage. Adv. Funct. Mater. 29(7), 1807753 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.201807753
                  
                " href="#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1516_3">50</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="G. Fang, Q. Wang, J. Zhou, Y. Lei et al., Metal organic framework-templated synthesis of bimetallic selenides with rich phase boundaries for sodium-ion storage and oxygen evolution reaction. ACS Nano 13(5), 5635–5645 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.9b00816
                  
                " href="#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1516_4">51</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Z. Ali, T. Tang, X. Huang, Y. Wang et al., Cobalt selenide decorated carbon spheres for excellent cycling performance of sodium ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 13, 19–28 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2017.12.014
                  
                " href="#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1516_5">52</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Y. Jiang, G. Zou, H. Hou, J. Li et al., Composition engineering boosts voltage windows for advanced sodium-ion batteries. ACS Nano 13(9), 10787–10797 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.9b05614
                  
                " href="#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1516_6">53</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="G. Fang, Z. Wu, J. Zhou, C. Zhu et al., Observation of pseudocapacitive effect and fast ion diffusion in bimetallic sulfides as an advanced sodium-ion battery anode. Adv. Energy Mater. 8(19), 1703155 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.201703155
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1519">54</a>]. The CSC can be cycled at high current densities (1 and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>) with excellent long-life cyclability, specifically, 410.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>anode</sub> at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> over 500 cycles without decay (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig2">2</a>h).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.3 </span>Electrochemical Kinetics</h3><p>The electrochemical kinetics of the CSC anode in half-cells is studied in detail by reference to the results of electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS). Compared with electrodes made from commercial samples of SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub>, the Nyquist curve for a typical CSC anode shows a semi-circle with smaller diameter, implying a faster charge transfer (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>a). Based on the derived equivalent circuit, the resistances of charge transfer for CSC, commercial SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> anodes are 9.5, 32.7, and 13.4 Ω, respectively (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>b). To compare Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (<span class="mathjax-tex">\(D_{{{\text{Na}}^{ + } }}\)</span>) in CSC and SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture, galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was conducted at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> for 0.5&nbsp;h, followed by relaxation for 2&nbsp;h. The typical GITT discharge profiles of CSC and SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture are shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>c. As illustrated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>d, <span class="mathjax-tex">\(D_{{{\text{Na}}^{ + } }}\)</span> can be calculated following equation <span class="mathjax-tex">\(D_{{{\text{Na}}^{ + } }} = \frac{{4L^{2} }}{\pi \tau }\left( {\frac{{\Delta E_{S} }}{{\Delta E_{t} }}} \right)^{2}\)</span>, where <i>L</i> is Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion length (cm), <i>τ</i> is the current impulse time (s), <i>t</i> is relaxation time (s), Δ<i>E</i><sub><i>S</i></sub> is steady-state potential change (V), Δ<i>E</i><sub><i>t</i></sub> is the instantaneous potential change (V) used to deduce IR drop [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="M. Hadouchi, N. Yaqoob, P. Kaghazchi, M. Tang et al., Fast sodium intercalation in Na3.41£0.59FeV(PO4)3: a novel sodium-deficient nasicon cathode for sodium-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 35, 192–202 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2020.11.010
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1754">55</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="J. Zhang, Y. Liu, X. Zhao, L. He et al., A novel NASICON-type Na4MnCr(PO4)3 demonstrating the energy density record of phosphate cathodes for sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 32(11), 1906348 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201906348
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1757">56</a>]. Corresponding to the GITT profiles, the calculated average <span class="mathjax-tex">\(D_{{{\text{Na}}^{ + } }}\)</span> is <i>ca.</i> 0.5 × 10<sup>–9</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, which is around twice that in half-cell with SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>e). Evidently, compared with simply mixed SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> anode, the CSC assembly of nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> particles shows remarkable superiority in terms of charge transfer kinetics and ionic diffusion.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Fig. 3"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 3</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Fig3_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig3" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Fig3_HTML.png" alt="figure 3" loading="lazy" width="685" height="520"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p><b>a</b> Nyquist plots of different anodes in half-cells and <b>b</b> corresponding equivalent circuit and charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>). <b>c</b> GITT profiles of Na//CSC half-cell discharged and <b>d</b> typical profile in a single GITT test. <b>e</b> Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient distribution corresponding to a typical discharge curve of Na//CSC half-cell (inset). <b>f</b> CV curves of Na//CSC half-cell at different scan rates. <b>g</b> <i>b</i>-values obtained by fitting peak current<i>-</i>scan rate correlation based on CV curves of Na//CSC half-cell. <b>h</b> Pseudocapacitive contribution (pseudocapa. contri.) of Na//CSC at different scan rates. <b>i</b> CV profiles of Na//CSC at 1.5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> and corresponding pseudocapacitive contribution (shaded region)</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 3" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Next, the pseudocapacitive contribution to charge storage in the Na//CSC half-cell was evaluated, on the basis that this component gives rise to faster charge transfer kinetics. CV curves at different rates are shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>f, and the correlation of peak currents (<i>i</i>) and scan rates (<i>v</i>) was assessed against the relationship <i>i</i> = <i>av</i><sup><i>b</i></sup>, where <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are adjustable constants [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="J. Wang, J. Polleux, J. Lim, B. Dunn, Pseudocapacitive contributions to electrochemical energy storage in TiO2 (anatase) nanoparticles. J. Phys. Chem. C 111(40), 14925–14931 (2007). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/jp074464w
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1904">57</a>]. As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>g, the resultant <i>b</i>-values are 0.98, 0.81, and 0.93, respectively, which implies the presence of a substantial pseudocapacitive contribution. The latter can be quantified through the equation <i>i</i> = <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> + <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>, where <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> represent pseudocapacitive and ion-diffusion controlled contribution, respectively [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="J. Wang, J. Polleux, J. Lim, B. Dunn, Pseudocapacitive contributions to electrochemical energy storage in TiO2 (anatase) nanoparticles. J. Phys. Chem. C 111(40), 14925–14931 (2007). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/jp074464w
                  
                " href="#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1944">57</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="C. An, Y. Yuan, B. Zhang, L. Tang et al., Graphene wrapped FeSe2 nano-microspheres with high pseudocapacitive contribution for enhanced Na-ion storage. Adv. Energy Mater. 9(18), 1900356 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.201900356
                  
                " href="#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1944_1">58</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Y. Tang, X. Li, H. Lv, W. Wang et al., High-energy aqueous magnesium hybrid full batteries enabled by carrier-hosting potential compensation. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 133(10), 5503–5512 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202013315
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e1947">59</a>]. As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>h, CSC anodes exhibit dominant pseudocapacitive contributions at scan rates of 0.1, 0.2, 0.4, 0.8, and 1.5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, specifically, 64.0%, 67.0%, 71.6%, 78.3%, and 86.3%, respectively. Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig3">3</a>i displays the CV curves of Na//CSC at 1.5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, in which the shaded region represents the pseudocapacitive contribution. This, together with the small charge transfer resistance and high <span class="mathjax-tex">\(D_{{{\text{Na}}^{ + } }}\)</span>, explains the excellent rate capability of the CSC anode.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.4 </span>Electrochemical Mechanism</h3><p>To investigate the mechanism that underpins the superior electrochemical behavior of CSC anodes, samples were at various states-of-(dis)charge characterized by ex situ XRD. The copper current collector in a Na//Cu half-cell discharged to 0.4&nbsp;V shows only the intrinsic diffraction peaks for metallic copper, verifying no evident electrochemical reaction between Na and Cu collector in ether-based electrolyte (Fig. S18). Compared with original samples (CSC, commercial SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub>), the samples after electrochemical activation exhibit dramatically different XRD patterns, indicating the occurrence of phase transition (Fig. S19). For CoS<sub>2</sub>, the relevant electrochemical reactions are as follows: CoS<sub>2</sub> + <i>x</i>Na<sup>+</sup>  + <i>x</i>e<sup>−</sup> → Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoS<sub>2</sub>, Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoS<sub>2</sub> + (4&nbsp;−&nbsp;<i>x</i>)Na<sup>+</sup>  + (4&nbsp;−&nbsp;<i>x</i>)e<sup>−</sup> ↔ 2Na<sub>2</sub>S + Co [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="X. Liu, K. Zhang, K. Lei, F. Li et al., Facile synthesis and electrochemical sodium storage of CoS2 micro/nano-structures. Nano Res. 9(1), 198–206 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s12274-016-0981-5
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2044">60</a>]. For SnS<sub>2</sub>, the corresponding electrochemical reactions are as follows: <i>x</i>Na<sup>+</sup>  + SnS<sub>2</sub> + <i>x</i>e<sup>−</sup> → Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>SnS<sub>2</sub>, Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>SnS<sub>2</sub> + (4-<i>x</i>)Na<sup>+</sup>  + (4-<i>x</i>)e<sup>−</sup> ↔ 2Na<sub>2</sub>S + Sn, Sn + yNa<sup>+</sup>  + ye<sup>−</sup> ↔ Na<sub>y</sub>Sn [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="L. Shi, D. Li, P. Yao, J. Yu et al., SnS2 nanosheets coating on nanohollow cubic CoS2/C for ultralong life and high rate capability half/full sodium-ion batteries. Small 14(41), 1802716 (2018). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.201802716
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2094">40</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="K. Zhang, Z. Hu, X. Liu, Z. Tao et al., FeSe2 microspheres as a high-performance anode material for na-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 27(21), 3305–3309 (2015). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201500196
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2097">61</a>]. Compared with single phases, the CSC anode shows similar featured diffraction peaks to pure SnS<sub>2</sub>, while the peaks from the CoS<sub>2</sub> diffraction pattern are difficult to discern. This could be associated with differences in crystallinity between products derived from SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub>. For investigating the mechanism of activated CSC, original CSC anodes were activated for at least 3 cycles to obtain phase-transformed materials. Corresponding to the discharge–charge-time curves in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>a, the activated CSC anodes at various states-of-charge show repeatable XRD patterns, implying good reversibility during the discharge/charge processes (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>b). The peak intensity of XRD pattern of anode (such as C-0.97&nbsp;V, blue) is lower than that of initially charged anode (such as C-0.97&nbsp;V, pink), which could be associated with the decreased diameter and gradually aggravated amorphization of metal sulfide phases. Similar phenomena have been reported in other metal chalcogenide anodes such as CoSe<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="K. Zhang, M. Park, L. Zhou, G.-H. Lee et al., Urchin-like CoSe2 as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 26(37), 6728–6735 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.201602608
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2119">13</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="X. Liu, K. Zhang, K. Lei, F. Li et al., Facile synthesis and electrochemical sodium storage of CoS2 micro/nano-structures. Nano Res. 9(1), 198–206 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s12274-016-0981-5
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2123">60</a>]. At different (dis)charge states, the corresponding XRD of anodes shows different patterns, which should be correlated to the successive formation of different products.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-4" data-title="Fig. 4"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig4" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 4</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/figures/4" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Fig4_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig4" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-021-00686-4/MediaObjects/40820_2021_686_Fig4_HTML.png" alt="figure 4" loading="lazy" width="685" height="748"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-4-desc"><p><b>a</b> Discharge–charge-time curve and <b>b</b> ex situ XRD patterns of CSC anode at different potentials. <b>c</b> HR-TEM image and <b>d</b> SAED pattern of CSC discharged to 0.4&nbsp;V. <b>e</b> HR-TEM image and <b>f</b> SAED pattern of CSC charged to 2.9&nbsp;V. <b>g</b> Schematic illustration of discharge/charge mechanisms of CSC anode. <b>h</b> Schematic illustration of reaction route and charge voltage change trend of CoS<sub>2</sub> anode. <b>i</b> Schematic illustration of reaction route and charge voltage change trend of CSC anode, showing cocktail mediation effect among nano-dispersed metal sulfide phases in CSC</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4/figures/4" data-track-dest="link:Figure4 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 4" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>c, HR-TEM image of CSC discharged to 0.4&nbsp;V displays interplanar spacings of 0.569 and 0.316&nbsp;nm, corresponding to lattice plane (0 0 4) of Na<sub>29.58</sub>Sn<sub>8</sub> and (1 0 1) of Co. Selected area electron diffraction (SAED) patterns reveal the lattice plane (2 1 1) of Co, (5 1 3) and (1 3 1) of Na<sub>29.58</sub>Sn<sub>8</sub> in the discharged product (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>d). When charged back to 2.9&nbsp;V, the crystalline domains in the resulting product are remarkably smaller than those in the discharged state. As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>e, HR-TEM image of CSC charged to 2.9&nbsp;V displays interplanar spacings of 0.184 and 0.295&nbsp;nm, which are assigned to lattice plane of (2 2 1)’ of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoS<sub>2</sub> and (0 0 2)’ of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>SnS<sub>2</sub> (with CoS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub> standard phases as reference), respectively. The SAED pattern exhibits typical polycrystalline features, in which lattice plane (2 2 0) of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>CoS<sub>2</sub>, (1 0 3) and (1 0 0) of Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>SnS<sub>2</sub> can be identified (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>f). Based on the characterization above, the progress of electrochemical reduction, followed by oxidation, for the CSC electrode is illustrated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>g. Typically, SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases in CSC experience an initial phase transition to Na<sup>+</sup>-intercalated intermediates (Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MS<sub>2</sub>, M = Sn, Co), which act as active materials for subsequent discharge/charge cycles. Based on the analysis above, the exotic property mediation beyond rule-of-mixtures [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="E.J. Pickering, N.G. Jones, High-entropy alloys: A critical assessment of their founding principles and future prospects. Int. Mater. Rev. 61(3), 183–202 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1080/09506608.2016.1180020
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2243">35</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Y. Ma, Y. Ma, Q. Wang, S. Schweidler et al., High-entropy energy materials: Challenges and new opportunities. Energy Environ. Sci. 14, 2883–2905 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/D1EE00505G
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2246">36</a>] (cocktail mediation effect) among nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases in CSC is schematically illustrated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>h–i. Specifically, along the different ionic diffusion directions, the nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases in CSC will alternatively react with Na<sup>+</sup> carriers, as schematically illustrated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig4">4</a>i. The nano-dispersion of SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases effectively shortens the ion diffusion path, which can kinetically boost electrochemical processes of both metal sulfide anodes. Due to intrinsic thermodynamics difference, the electrochemical competition is present between SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases. Also, it does not exclude one of the two phases could show local kinetic merit owing to the diameter difference between them. Thus, in the CSC anode, the alternative electrochemical reaction processes could coexist between the two phases. It enables complementary charge voltage plateau of different metal sulfide phases, resulting in lowered charge plateau of CSC anode.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.5 </span>Full-Cell Properties</h3><p>To verify the practicability of the CSC anode, a high-voltage cathode material Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> was employed to assemble CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cells. Synthesis of Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> followed a modified literature method (Supporting Information), and yielded a micro-particle morphology with a well-matched XRD pattern with the standard phase (Fig. S20) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Y. Xu, W. Cao, Y. Yin, J. Sheng et al., Novel NaTi2(PO4)3 nanowire clusters as high performance cathodes for mg-na hybrid-ion batteries. Nano Energy 55, 526–533 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.nanoen.2018.10.064
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2303">33</a>]. Corresponding to CV curves, Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> cathode shows <i>ca.</i> 3.9&nbsp;V discharge plateau with low electrochemical polarization, which is suitable for demonstrating the practicability of different anodes (Fig. S21a, b). The Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> cathode delivers a good rate capability from 0.05 to 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, showing a high reversible capacity of 124.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub> at 0.05 A/g (Fig. S21c, d). Over 350 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> cathode shows a capacity of 106.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub>, corresponding to a low capacity decay of 0.02% per cycle (Fig. S22). Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig5">5</a>a shows the typical CV curves of CoS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub>, SnS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub>, and CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cells at 0.5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. Evidently, the main redox peaks of CoS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> appear at 1.0–2.5&nbsp;V, implying that its average discharge voltage is in the range. In contrast, the ranges of main redox peaks of SnS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> and CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cells are in 2.0–4.0&nbsp;V, which imply a higher average discharge voltage than that of the former. Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig5">5</a>b shows that the discharge capacity available from the CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> cell, while the voltage is above 2&nbsp;V, is <i>ca.</i> 61.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub>, which is 1.62 times that of CoS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub>. As displayed in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig5">5</a>c, CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cells present an average discharge voltage of 2.57&nbsp;V, which is close to that of SnS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> and <i>ca.</i> 0.62&nbsp;V higher than that with CoS<sub>2</sub> anode. The CSC anode confers a significantly higher average voltage during discharge of full-cells when compared with CoS<sub>2</sub> cells. Compared with other full-cells reported previously, CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cells also show obvious merits in terms of discharge voltage and capacity (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig5">5</a>d). Moreover, CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cells show a high-rate capability from 0.05 to 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, delivering a high capacity of 120.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub> at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig5">5</a>e). The corresponding discharge/charge curves are shown in Fig. S23, where the voltage plateaus are well-retained. As exhibited in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig5">5</a>f, compared with other full-cells with different electrode materials, CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cell delivers comparable merits in terms of energy/power density. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="L. Liang, Y. Xu, C. Wang, L. Wen et al., Large-scale highly ordered sb nanorod array anodes with high capacity and rate capability for sodium-ion batteries. Energy Environ. Sci. 8(10), 2954–2962 (2015). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/C5EE00878F
                  
                " href="#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2480">62</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="P.                   https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.nanolett.8b05189
                  
                " href="#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2480_1">63</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="N.                   https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201505918
                  
                " href="#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2480_2">64</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="J.                   https://doi.org/10.1002/smtd.201800371
                  
                " href="#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2480_4">66</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="H.                   https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202001418
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d86128253e2484">67</a>] Specifically, ~106.1 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub>/1278.3&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub> are achieved at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. When operated over 120 cycles at 0.25 A g<sup>−1</sup>, CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cell shows a high capacity of 63.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub> with a low decay of 0.20% per cycle (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-021-00686-4#Fig5">5</a>g). Such results suggest a good practicability of CSC in full-cells.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" CoS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub>, SnS<sub>2</sub>//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub>, and CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cells at 0.5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. <b>b</b> Corresponding discharge/charge curves and <b>c</b> discharge plateaus of full-cells at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>. <b>d</b> Discharge aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></section><section data-title="Conclusions"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec9-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec9"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3 </span>Conclusions</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec9-content"><p>Despite with high-capacity and low-cost merits, the ubiquitous low-rate and high-plateau issues greatly lower the practicability of metal sulfide anodes in full-cells. Herein, enlightened by electrolyte/structure-dependent properties of metal sulfides, CSC anode assembled by nano-dispersed SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub> phases is engineered as a case study in ether-based electrolyte, simultaneously realizing high-rate and low-plateau properties. The high nano-dispersity of metal sulfides endows CSC anode with evident cocktail mediation effect similar to high-entropy materials, effectively circumventing intrinsic drawbacks of different metal sulfides. The utilized ether-based electrolyte greatly enhances the reversibility of metal sulfides, sustaining a long-life effectivity of cocktail-like mediation. In half-cells, CSC delivers an ultrahigh-rate capability of 327.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>anode</sub> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup> and remarkably lowered average charge voltage up to <i>ca.</i> 0.62&nbsp;V, far outperforming CoS<sub>2</sub> phase and SnS<sub>2</sub>/CoS<sub>2</sub> mixture. The as-assembled CSC//Na<sub>1.5</sub>VPO<sub>4.8</sub>F<sub>0.7</sub> full-cell shows a good rate capability (0.05–1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, 120.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup><sub>electrode</sub> at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and a high average discharge voltage up to 2.57&nbsp;V, comparable to full-cells with alloy-type anodes. Kinetics and mechanism studies further verify that the cocktail-like mediation effect largely boosts charge transfer and ionic diffusion in CSC, while alternative and complementary electrochemical processes between different nano-dispersed metal sulfides (SnS<sub>2</sub> and CoS<sub>2</sub>) and Na<sup>+</sup> carriers account for the lowered charge plateau of CSC. This work shows a unique electrolyte/structure-dependent cocktail-like mediation effect of metal sulfide anodes, which will boost the development of high-rate/-voltage sodium-ion full batteries.</p></div></div></section>
                                </div>
